This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a cybertextual data structure that was a map of itself. Dante Alighieri must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Dante Alighieri chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Dante Alighieri entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dante Alighieri felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a library that had never known the light of the sun. Socrates had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Socrates walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Socrates entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Socrates discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Socrates entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Socrates wandered, lost in thought. 

Socrates entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Socrates opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Socrates entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Socrates muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Socrates entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Socrates walked away from that place. Quite unexpectedly Socrates reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twilight dimention in space from which few emerged. Scheherazade was almost certain about why she happened to be there. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Scheherazade discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. At the darkest hour Scheherazade found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a mysterious labyrinth that lived in eternal twilight. Kublai Khan must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. Quite unexpectedly Kublai Khan discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twisted garden that lived in eternal twilight. Dante Alighieri couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a cramped and narrow peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Dante Alighieri entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dante Alighieri opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. Quite unexpectedly Dante Alighieri reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

Once upon a time, there was a philosopher named Socrates, a blind poet named Homer and a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri. This is the story that Homer told:

There was once a recursive house of many doors from which few emerged. Homer couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Homer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Homer entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way.

Homer entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Homer entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer walked away from that place. 

Homer entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Homer entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. At the darkest hour Homer discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Homer said, ending his story.

"And that was how it happened," Scheherazade said, ending her story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri, a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo and a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan. Kublai Khan suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Kublai Khan told:

There was once a recursive house of many doors that was also this story as I tell it to you. Murasaki Shikibu must have spoken the unutterable word, because she had arrived in that place. Murasaki Shikibu opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a fogou, dominated by a lararium which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Murasaki Shikibu walked away from that place. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Murasaki Shikibu wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a liwan, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Murasaki Shikibu felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Murasaki Shikibu felt sure that this must be the way out.

This is the story that Kublai Khan told:

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a queen of Persia named Scheherazade and a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges. Scheherazade suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an architectural forest from which few emerged. Marco Polo couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought. 

Marco Polo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a cramped and narrow terrace, dominated by a fallen column which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Marco Polo entered a rough terrace, dominated by a lararium which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought. 

Marco Polo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo walked away from that place. 

Marco Polo entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, tastefully offset by moki steps. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. And there Marco Polo reached the end of the labyrinth.

This is the story that Marco Polo told:

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a philosopher named Socrates and a king of Persia named Shahryar. Socrates suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Socrates told:

There was once a library with many forking paths. Kublai Khan wasn't quite sure where this was, only that he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, dominated by a sipapu which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. 

Kublai Khan entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a lararium. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a moasic. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. At the darkest hour Kublai Khan reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Socrates ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Socrates told:

There was once an engmatic labyrinth with many forking paths. Shahryar didn't know why he happened to be there. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Shahryar entered a rough fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Shahryar entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Shahryar entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a lararium. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Shahryar entered a high peristyle, dominated by a lararium framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Shahryar entered a high peristyle, dominated by a lararium framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar wandered, lost in thought. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Shahryar entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Shahryar entered a high terrace, dominated by a koi pond which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Shahryar entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Shahryar opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Shahryar entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Shahryar entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a lararium. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Shahryar entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. Almost unable to believe it, Shahryar found the exit.

"And that was how it happened," Socrates said, ending his story.

"And that was how it happened," Marco Polo said, ending his story.

"And that was how it happened," Geoffery Chaucer said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a philosopher named Socrates, an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer and a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri. Geoffery Chaucer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Geoffery Chaucer told:

Once upon a time, there was an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo, a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Jorges Luis Borges suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Jorges Luis Borges told:

There was once an engmatic labyrinth that had never known the light of the sun. Dunyazad was lost, like so many before and after, and she had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dunyazad walked away from that place. 

Dunyazad entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dunyazad entered a luxurious liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dunyazad entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Dunyazad wandered, lost in thought. 

Dunyazad entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a rough terrace, tastefully offset by a fountain. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Dunyazad chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Dunyazad entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a luxurious liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dunyazad entered a luxurious liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dunyazad discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dunyazad entered a cramped and narrow terrace, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dunyazad discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. Which was where Dunyazad found the exit.

Then Jorges Luis Borges ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Jorges Luis Borges opened his book and read them the following page:

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges, an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer and a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan. Geoffery Chaucer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Geoffery Chaucer told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Geoffery Chaucer said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad, a poet of Rome named Virgil and a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu. Virgil suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Virgil told:

There was once an architectural forest from which few emerged. Kublai Khan couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow peristyle, dominated by a sipapu framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. And there Kublai Khan discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Virgil said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a poet of Rome named Virgil, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu. Virgil suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Virgil told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Virgil said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone just on the other side of the garden wall. Dante Alighieri had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri wandered, lost in thought. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. Almost unable to believe it, Dante Alighieri discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri, a philosopher named Socrates and a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo. Socrates suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Socrates told:

Once upon a time, there was a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri, a blind poet named Homer and a poet of Rome named Virgil. Dante Alighieri suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:

Once upon a time, there was a philosopher named Socrates, a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Murasaki Shikibu suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Murasaki Shikibu told:

Once upon a time, there was a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan, a blind poet named Homer and a king of Persia named Shahryar. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Homer told:

There was once an architectural forest that was also this story as I tell it to you. Virgil couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Virgil discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Virgil entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Virgil muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Virgil entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Virgil felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. At the darkest hour Virgil discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Homer said, ending his story.

Then Murasaki Shikibu ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Murasaki Shikibu opened her book and read them the following page:

Then Murasaki Shikibu ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Murasaki Shikibu told:

There was once a twisted garden from which few emerged. Socrates couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Socrates thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Socrates entered a rough peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Socrates discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Socrates entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Socrates chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Socrates entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Socrates felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Socrates entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Socrates felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. Almost unable to believe it, Socrates discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Murasaki Shikibu said, ending her story.

Then Dante Alighieri ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Dante Alighieri said, ending his story.

"And that was how it happened," Socrates said, ending his story.

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:

Once upon a time, there was a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges. Dante Alighieri suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. Then Dante Alighieri ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:

There was once a twilight dimention in space that some call the unknown. Kublai Khan had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. 

Kublai Khan entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow terrace, dominated by a fallen column which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a koi pond with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a koi pond with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. Almost unable to believe it, Kublai Khan found the exit.

Then Dante Alighieri ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:

Once upon a time, there was a queen of Persia named Scheherazade, a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo and a king of Persia named Shahryar. Scheherazade suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone that was a map of itself. Jorges Luis Borges was lost, like so many before and after, and he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by a fallen column which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a moasic. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a moasic. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a fogou, tastefully offset by moki steps. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high peristyle, dominated by divans lining the perimeter framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, dominated by a moasic with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough kiva, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough kiva, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. At the darkest hour Jorges Luis Borges found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a library with many forking paths. Geoffery Chaucer couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Geoffery Chaucer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Geoffery Chaucer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Geoffery Chaucer wandered, lost in thought. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a moasic. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Geoffery Chaucer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Geoffery Chaucer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps.

"And that was how it happened," Dante Alighieri said, ending his story.

Then Dante Alighieri ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:

There was once a recursive house of many doors that lived in eternal twilight. Dante Alighieri didn't know why he happened to be there. Dante Alighieri walked away from that place. 

Dante Alighieri entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Dante Alighieri entered a liwan, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Dante Alighieri chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. At the darkest hour Dante Alighieri reached the end of the labyrinth.

"And that was how it happened," Dante Alighieri said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an architectural forest that was also this story as I tell it to you. Virgil couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Virgil discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Virgil entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of arabseque. Virgil muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Virgil entered a luxurious liwan, dominated by a lararium framed by a pattern of arabseque. Virgil felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Virgil entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Virgil felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. Almost unable to believe it, Virgil found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a library with many forking paths. Homer was lost, like so many before and after, and he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Homer entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Homer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Homer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Homer entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Homer entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Homer wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Homer discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Homer told:

Once upon a time, there was a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo, a queen of Persia named Scheherazade and a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges. Jorges Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Jorges Luis Borges opened his book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Homer told:

There was once a library with many forking paths. Dunyazad must have spoken the unutterable word, because she had arrived in that place. Dunyazad discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a high fogou, dominated by moki steps which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad wandered, lost in thought. 

Dunyazad entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dunyazad walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dunyazad entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dunyazad entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dunyazad walked away from that place. 

Dunyazad entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Dunyazad discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dunyazad entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. At the darkest hour Dunyazad found the exit.

Then Homer ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges, a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan and a philosopher named Socrates. Jorges Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Jorges Luis Borges told:

Once upon a time, there was a king of Persia named Shahryar, an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo and a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan. Kublai Khan suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Kublai Khan told:

There was once a twilight dimention in space from which few emerged. Little Nemo had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Little Nemo walked away from that place. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Little Nemo entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Little Nemo walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Little Nemo entered a cramped and narrow peristyle, tastefully offset by moki steps. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low kiva, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a rough liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a rough liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Little Nemo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way.

"And that was how it happened," Jorges Luis Borges said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a recursive house of many doors, which is the world. Jorges Luis Borges must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough fogou, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough kiva, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by a sipapu which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough terrace, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought. Almost unable to believe it, Jorges Luis Borges discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twisted garden that lived in eternal twilight. Geoffery Chaucer was lost, like so many before and after, and he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Geoffery Chaucer wandered, lost in thought. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Geoffery Chaucer walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Geoffery Chaucer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Geoffery Chaucer walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Geoffery Chaucer walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. Quite unexpectedly Geoffery Chaucer reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad, a philosopher named Socrates and a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu. Socrates suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Socrates opened his book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twisted garden that lived in eternal twilight. Marco Polo didn't know why he happened to be there. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought. 

Marco Polo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Marco Polo entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Marco Polo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Marco Polo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Marco Polo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Marco Polo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. And there Marco Polo reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Marco Polo told:

There was once a mysterious labyrinth that some call the unknown. Little Nemo was almost certain about why he happened to be there. Little Nemo walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Little Nemo entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Little Nemo discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Marco Polo said, ending his story.

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence.

There was once a cybertextual data structure that had never known the light of the sun. Jorges Luis Borges didn't know why he happened to be there. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. Almost unable to believe it, Jorges Luis Borges found the exit.

There was once an architectural forest that was also this story as I tell it to you. Jorges Luis Borges must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a fogou, dominated by a fallen column which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. And there Jorges Luis Borges discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Marco Polo said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a recursive house of many doors from which few emerged. Shahryar couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Shahryar entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a rough fogou, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Shahryar wandered, lost in thought. 

Shahryar entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Shahryar walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Shahryar entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Shahryar entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Shahryar entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Shahryar entered a high fogou, dominated by a sipapu which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Shahryar entered a high fogou, dominated by a sipapu which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Shahryar entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Shahryar entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Shahryar entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, tastefully offset by moki steps. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, tastefully offset by moki steps. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Shahryar entered a luxurious liwan, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. At the darkest hour Shahryar discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."
