So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo, a blind poet named Homer and a philosopher named Socrates. Little Nemo suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Little Nemo told:

There was once an architectural forest that some call the unknown. Geoffery Chaucer couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Geoffery Chaucer wandered, lost in thought. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a cramped and narrow peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a lararium. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Geoffery Chaucer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Geoffery Chaucer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a kiva, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a luxurious kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Geoffery Chaucer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer wandered, lost in thought. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer walked away from that place. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Geoffery Chaucer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a fogou, dominated by an obelisk which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer walked away from that place. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Geoffery Chaucer walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high terrace, dominated by a koi pond which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a rough peristyle, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a cramped and narrow peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high terrace, tastefully offset by a moasic. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out. And there Geoffery Chaucer discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Little Nemo said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone, a place where many had become lost. Kublai Khan wasn't quite sure where this was, only that he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough fogou, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Kublai Khan entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious liwan, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough fogou, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Kublai Khan thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. Which was where Kublai Khan reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twilight dimention in space, which is the world. Homer wasn't quite sure where this was, only that he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Homer wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Homer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Homer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Homer entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Homer entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Homer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Homer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Homer wandered, lost in thought. 

Homer entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Homer walked away from that place. 

Homer entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Homer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Homer entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Homer walked away from that place. 

Homer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Homer entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Homer walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. Quite unexpectedly Homer found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twisted garden, which is the world. Marco Polo had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo walked away from that place. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Marco Polo entered a rough fogou, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Marco Polo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Marco Polo walked away from that place. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Marco Polo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Marco Polo entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Marco Polo walked away from that place. 

Marco Polo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Marco Polo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Marco Polo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Marco Polo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. Which was where Marco Polo found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an engmatic labyrinth with many forking paths. Scheherazade must have gotten lost, because she was wandering there. Scheherazade discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Scheherazade entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Scheherazade walked away from that place. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a rough kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of arabseque. Scheherazade walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. Quite unexpectedly Scheherazade found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer, the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad and a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan. Geoffery Chaucer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Geoffery Chaucer told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Geoffery Chaucer said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a philosopher named Socrates and a queen of Persia named Scheherazade. Scheherazade suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a philosopher named Socrates, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu. Murasaki Shikibu suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Murasaki Shikibu told:

Once upon a time, there was a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan, a philosopher named Socrates and a queen of Persia named Scheherazade. Socrates suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Socrates opened his book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Murasaki Shikibu told:

There was once an architectural forest that some call the unknown. Geoffery Chaucer was almost certain about why he happened to be there. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a rough terrace, tastefully offset by a fountain. Geoffery Chaucer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a rough peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. At the darkest hour Geoffery Chaucer found the exit.

"And that was how it happened," Murasaki Shikibu said, ending her story.

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twilight dimention in space that was also this story as I tell it to you. Scheherazade couldn't quite say how she was wandering there. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought. 

Scheherazade entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Scheherazade entered a rough liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Scheherazade entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. At the darkest hour Scheherazade found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a library with many forking paths. Homer must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Homer entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Homer entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of arabseque. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Homer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Homer entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Homer entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way. And there Homer found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

Then Geoffery Chaucer ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Geoffery Chaucer told:

Once upon a time, there was a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu, the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad and a philosopher named Socrates. Murasaki Shikibu suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Murasaki Shikibu told a very exciting story. Then Murasaki Shikibu ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Murasaki Shikibu told a very exciting story. Then Murasaki Shikibu ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Murasaki Shikibu opened her book and read them the following page:

Then Murasaki Shikibu ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Murasaki Shikibu told:

Once upon a time, there was the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad, a philosopher named Socrates and a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri. Socrates suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Socrates told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Socrates said, ending his story.

Then Murasaki Shikibu ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Murasaki Shikibu told:

There was once an expansive zone, the place that can sometimes be glimpsed through mirrors. Socrates must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Socrates discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Socrates entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Socrates entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates wandered, lost in thought. 

Socrates entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Socrates walked away from that place. 

Socrates entered a cramped and narrow kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of arabseque. Socrates opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Socrates entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Socrates entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Socrates felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Socrates entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Socrates muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Socrates entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Socrates felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Socrates entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Socrates discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Socrates entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a lararium. Socrates walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Socrates entered a rough liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Socrates entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Socrates walked away from that place. 

Socrates entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Socrates felt sure that this must be the way out. At the darkest hour Socrates reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Murasaki Shikibu ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Murasaki Shikibu opened her book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a queen of Persia named Scheherazade. Scheherazade suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a poet of Rome named Virgil, a blind poet named Homer and a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo. Little Nemo suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Little Nemo told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Little Nemo said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Scheherazade suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an architectural forest from which few emerged. Dunyazad wasn't quite sure where this was, only that she had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dunyazad entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dunyazad wandered, lost in thought. 

Dunyazad entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Dunyazad thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Dunyazad reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twilight dimention in space, which is the world. Little Nemo must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Little Nemo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo walked away from that place. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo walked away from that place. Quite unexpectedly Little Nemo found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twilight dimention in space that contained the entire world. Shahryar must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Shahryar entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Shahryar entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Shahryar wandered, lost in thought. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. Quite unexpectedly Shahryar reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri, a blind poet named Homer and an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Homer told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Homer said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a vast and perilous maze, the place that can sometimes be glimpsed through mirrors. Jorges Luis Borges was lost, like so many before and after, and he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low fogou, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, dominated by a lararium with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. Which was where Jorges Luis Borges discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a queen of Persia named Scheherazade, a king of Persia named Shahryar and a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges. Jorges Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Jorges Luis Borges told a very exciting story. Then Jorges Luis Borges ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Jorges Luis Borges told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Jorges Luis Borges said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a twisted garden that lived in eternal twilight. Virgil must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Virgil chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Virgil entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Virgil walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Virgil entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Virgil felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Virgil entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Virgil muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Virgil entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Virgil entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil walked away from that place. 

Virgil entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Virgil entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Virgil felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Virgil entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Virgil opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Virgil entered a cramped and narrow fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Virgil chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Virgil entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Virgil muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. And there Virgil discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone, the place that can sometimes be glimpsed through mirrors. Scheherazade didn't know why she happened to be there. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Scheherazade discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of acanthus. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Scheherazade entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Scheherazade entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Scheherazade chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Scheherazade entered a fogou, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a rough kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of arabseque. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence.

Scheherazade entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Scheherazade entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Scheherazade discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Scheherazade entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of acanthus. Scheherazade walked away from that place. 

Scheherazade entered a rough terrace, tastefully offset by a fountain. Scheherazade walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Scheherazade entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Scheherazade chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Scheherazade entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought. 

Scheherazade entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought. 

Scheherazade entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. At the darkest hour Scheherazade found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone with many forking paths. Shahryar had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. At the darkest hour Shahryar discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad, a blind poet named Homer and an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Homer told:

Once upon a time, there was the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad, a philosopher named Socrates and a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu. Murasaki Shikibu suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an architectural forest from which few emerged. Jorges Luis Borges must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way. Which was where Jorges Luis Borges discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone, a place where many had become lost. Jorges Luis Borges was almost certain about why he happened to be there. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough terrace, tastefully offset by a fountain. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Jorges Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high fogou, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a rough liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Jorges Luis Borges opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought. Which was where Jorges Luis Borges discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a library that had never known the light of the sun. Little Nemo didn't know why he happened to be there. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Little Nemo entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo walked away from that place. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Little Nemo entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Little Nemo entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Little Nemo discovered the way out.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a recursive house of many doors that some call the unknown. Dunyazad was almost certain about why she happened to be there. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dunyazad thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Dunyazad entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dunyazad thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low fogou, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dunyazad entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dunyazad opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Dunyazad entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dunyazad entered a peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. At the darkest hour Dunyazad found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a philosopher named Socrates, a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan and a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges. Kublai Khan suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Kublai Khan told:

There was once a twisted garden that was also this story as I tell it to you. Kublai Khan was almost certain about why he happened to be there. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. Quite unexpectedly Kublai Khan discovered the way out.

"And that was how it happened," Kublai Khan said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Jorges Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Jorges Luis Borges told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Jorges Luis Borges said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone with many forking paths. Geoffery Chaucer must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. At the darkest hour Geoffery Chaucer found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo, an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Little Nemo suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Little Nemo told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Little Nemo said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a vast and perilous maze, the place that can sometimes be glimpsed through mirrors. Kublai Khan must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. At the darkest hour Kublai Khan reached the end of the labyrinth.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

Once upon a time, there was the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad, a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges and a poet of Rome named Virgil. Virgil suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Virgil told:

Once upon a time, there was a philosopher named Socrates, a poet of Rome named Virgil and a blind librarian named Jorges Luis Borges. Socrates suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Socrates opened his book and read them the following page:

Then Socrates ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Socrates told:

There was once a library that was a map of itself. Jorges Luis Borges had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Jorges Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by moki steps with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorges Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Jorges Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Jorges Luis Borges entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorges Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Jorges Luis Borges found the exit.

Then Socrates ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Socrates opened his book and read them the following page:

"And that was how it happened," Little Nemo said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once an expansive zone just on the other side of the garden wall. Socrates had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Socrates wandered, lost in thought. 

Socrates entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Socrates felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Socrates entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Socrates felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Socrates entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Socrates felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Socrates entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Socrates discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Socrates entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Socrates felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Socrates entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Socrates walked away from that place. 

Socrates entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Socrates muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Socrates entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Socrates entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Socrates entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of arabseque. Socrates muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Socrates entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates wandered, lost in thought. 

Socrates entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Socrates wandered, lost in thought. 

Socrates entered a fogou, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Socrates wandered, lost in thought. 

Socrates entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by divans lining the perimeter framed by a pattern of acanthus. Socrates wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. And there Socrates found the exit.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." Then Scheherazade opened her book and read them the following page:

Then Marco Polo ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Marco Polo told a very exciting story. Then Marco Polo ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Marco Polo told:

Once upon a time, there was an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer, the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad and a queen of Persia named Scheherazade. Scheherazade suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

There was once a vast and perilous maze, a place where many had become lost. Homer must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Homer entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Homer entered a liwan, dominated by divans lining the perimeter framed by a pattern of arabseque. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Homer entered a liwan, dominated by divans lining the perimeter framed by a pattern of arabseque. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Homer entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Homer walked away from that place. 

Homer entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Homer walked away from that place. 

Homer entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Homer entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a moasic. Homer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Homer entered a luxurious kiva, tastefully offset by moki steps. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Homer entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a cramped and narrow peristyle, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Homer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Homer entered a rough kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of arabseque. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Homer entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. Almost unable to believe it, Homer reached the end of the labyrinth.

"And that was how it happened," Scheherazade said, ending her story.

Then Marco Polo ended his story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Marco Polo told:

There was once a cybertextual data structure that had never known the light of the sun. Shahryar was almost certain about why he happened to be there. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Shahryar entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Shahryar entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out. And there Shahryar reached the end of the labyrinth.

"And that was how it happened," Marco Polo said, ending his story.

Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Then Scheherazade ended her story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."
